❯ Yes, if it is easy to fix, we can automate it.  Is the fix a local gitconfig  
thing that must be copied to my other mac computer afterwards?                  

⏺ No, it's not a global gitconfig change. It's per-clone — each repo's
  .git/config stores its remote URL. So the fix is just git remote set-url 
  origin git@github.com:... in each repo. Since the script runs on both
  machines, we can have it auto-fix on whichever machine it runs on.

  The conversion is simple: take the existing URL, extract the owner/repo.git
  path, and rewrite it as git@github.com:owner/repo.git. This handles the cases
  where the local directory name differs from the GitHub repo name (e.g.,
  abohlib → abohlib_ada, hybrid_app_docs → docs_app).

  Let me update the script.

❯ great! so, the config is preserved in the remote, too?                        

⏺ No — the remote URL is stored only in each local clone's .git/config. GitHub
  doesn't know or care which protocol you use to connect.

  So you'll need to run this script on both machines. The first run on each
  machine converts the HTTPS remotes to SSH, and subsequent runs just fetch and
  pull.

❯ sorry...  I meant when we push to the remote, does the repo's local           
.git/config file get pushed to gh?                                              

⏺ No. The .git/ directory is never pushed — it's purely local metadata. GitHub
  never sees your remote URLs, credentials, or local git config.

  So each machine's clones are independent. The script handles this by
  auto-fixing on every run.
❯ I am actually wondering what is the best way to have uniformity across all of 
 the repos I create locally and eventually push most to gh?  when cloning from  
gh, it sounds like the repo/.git/config is either automatically created or      
doesn't exist.                                                                  

⏺ When you clone, Git creates .git/config automatically and sets the origin
  remote URL to whatever protocol you used to clone:

  - git clone git@github.com:... → SSH remote
  - git clone https://github.com/... → HTTPS remote

  So the simplest way to get uniformity is to always clone via SSH. But you can
  also configure Git globally to force SSH for all GitHub URLs, regardless of
  how you clone:

  git config --global url."git@github.com:".insteadOf "https://github.com/"

  This rewrites any HTTPS GitHub URL to SSH automatically — for clone, fetch,
  pull, push, everything. It goes in your ~/.gitconfig on each machine, so you'd
   set it once on the Mac Pro and once on the MacBook Pro. After that, even if
  you paste an HTTPS URL from a browser, Git uses SSH.

  Want me to set that up on this machine?

you can read it, but I think it is okay.                                        

  Read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

⏺ Looks clean. The url.insteadOf rewrite isn't there. Want me to add it so all
  future GitHub operations automatically use SSH?

  [url "git@github.com:"]
      insteadOf = https://github.com/

  That plus the script's auto-fix for existing clones would cover both past and
  future repos.

❯ So, in the repo's .git/config file, the local git client or gh is injecting   
defaults for anything not in my user level .gitconfig.                          

⏺ Exactly. Git uses a layered config hierarchy:

  1. System (/etc/gitconfig) — machine-wide defaults
  2. User (~/.gitconfig) — your global settings
  3. Repo (.git/config) — per-clone overrides

  Lower levels override higher. When you clone, Git creates .git/config with
  just the remote URL and branch tracking info — the minimum needed for that
  clone. Everything else (your name, email, GPG signing, colors, etc.) is
  inherited from your user-level config.

  So yes — add the insteadOf rewrite to ~/.gitconfig and every clone on that
  machine will use SSH automatically, without needing anything in each repo's
  .git/config. Want me to add it?

❯ great explanation. thanks!  so, let's add the change to my user level git     
config.

❯ i keep the development environments identical (goal), so the source is in the 
 same user and path, the user account is the same name, etc.  Would it make     
more sense when I switch from macpro to work on macbook, to use rsync           
(scripted) to ensure that critical configuration and source files are the same  
between the systems.  1. macpro your script fetch, git, push as long as there   
are no issues, else reverts and reports for all the repositories of interest.   
2. Command in the script or additional step that will use rsync to copy new or  
changed files from macpro to macbook.  the assumption being that macpro is the  
gold master without any known issues.  rsync could and probably should only     
sync local configuration files since the git script will be run to fetch pull   
from gh on the macbook.  what do you think?  I am thinking of $HOME/.zshrc,     
.gitconfig, each of the repos of interest .git/config and exports folder for    
each repo, if it exists.  no coding, just thinking                              

⏺ Good thinking. A few observations:

  What rsync makes sense for (not in git, must be identical):
  - ~/.gitconfig — identical across both machines
  - ~/.zshrc — mostly identical, but watch out for machine-specific aliases
  (adat on Mac Pro vs adast on MacBook Pro)
  - exports/ folders — if these contain shared config or artifacts not in git

  What rsync does NOT make sense for:
  - ~/.ssh/config — different identity files per machine (id_mike_macpro_gh vs
  id_mike_macbook_gh), so a blind copy would break SSH on the MacBook Pro
  - Repo .git/config files — the global insteadOf rule plus the script's
  auto-fix already handles this; rsyncing these could overwrite branch tracking
  differences
  - Source code — GitHub is the sync mechanism, not rsync

  Potential issue with .zshrc:
  If both machines have identical shell configs, great. But if there are
  machine-specific entries (Docker aliases, PATH differences for Alire vs system
   GNAT), you'd want either a shared .zshrc that sources a machine-specific
  .zshrc.local, or just exclude it from rsync.

  My recommendation:
  Keep the sync narrow — ~/.gitconfig and maybe exports/ folders. Let the git
  update script handle all repo state. For .zshrc and .ssh/config, those are
  machine-specific enough that manual management (or a shared dotfiles repo) is
  safer than rsync.

  What do you think?

❯ gh is the source of Truth.                                                    

⏺ Right. Two things to address:

  1. Global pull strategy — add pull.rebase = false (or pull.ff = only) to
  ~/.gitconfig so Git doesn't prompt about reconciliation every time.
  2. Script improvement — since GitHub is the source of truth, the script should
   detect divergence and reset to origin/main rather than failing. If the local
  branch has uncommitted or unpushed work, warn and exit instead.

  Want me to set the global pull strategy to fast-forward only (which will fail
  cleanly on divergence), and then update the script to handle divergence by
  resetting to the remote?

❯ what is the best practice and safe choice?                                    

⏺ pull.ff = only (fast-forward only) is the safest choice.

  - Normal case (no local divergence): pull succeeds silently, just like now.
  - Divergence detected: pull fails cleanly instead of silently creating merge
  commits or rebasing your work.
  - You decide: when it fails, you consciously choose what to do — reset to
  remote, rebase, or merge.

  No surprises, no silent rewrites. The script can then catch the failure and
  handle it appropriately since GitHub is the source of truth.

  Want me to set it globally and update the script?

❯ this area of git is vague to me.  assuming that any choice can always be      
undone or reverted, what choice do you like?                                    

⏺ I'd go with pull.ff = only for the same reasons:

  - It's the Git project's own recommended default (they added it as a hint for
  a reason)
  - It never silently does something unexpected — it either cleanly
  fast-forwards or stops and tells you
  - In your workflow (two machines, GitHub is truth), 99% of pulls will be clean
   fast-forwards and just work
  - The 1% where it fails means something unexpected happened, and you want to
  know about it rather than have Git guess

  And yes, anything can be undone — git reflog preserves everything for 90 days
  regardless of what happens.

  Shall I set it and update the script?

❯ Okay, we need to remember to manually sync the mbp's gitconfig                

⏺ Bash(git config --global pull.ff only)
  ⎿  (No output)

⏺ Done. For the MacBook Pro, you'll need to run these two commands:

  git config --global pull.ff only
  git config --global url."git@github.com:".insteadOf "https://github.com/"

  Now let me update the script to handle divergence properly, then rerun it.

⏺ Yes, the SSH auto-fix is still in there (ensure_ssh_remote). The script now
  does five things per repo:

  1. Convert HTTPS remote to SSH if needed
  2. Switch to main if on a different branch
  3. Fetch from remote
  4. Set upstream tracking if missing
  5. Reset to origin/main on divergence (if no uncommitted changes), otherwise
  normal pull

  locally

⏺ Based on the current .zshrc:

  ┌──────────────────────────────┬────────────────┬───────┐
  │           Command            │ amd64 (x86_64) │ arm64 │
  ├──────────────────────────────┼────────────────┼───────┤
  │ adat (Alire toolchain)       │      yes       │  no   │
  ├──────────────────────────────┼────────────────┼───────┤

  ├──────────────────────────────┼────────────────┼───────┤

  ├──────────────────────────────┼────────────────┼───────┤

  ├──────────────────────────────┼────────────────┼───────┤
  │ got (Go container)           │      yes       │  yes  │
  ├──────────────────────────────┼────────────────┼───────┤
  │ rustt (Rust container)       │      yes       │  yes  │
  └──────────────────────────────┴────────────────┴───────┘

  Only adat is gated — everything else is available on both architectures.

  network, image doesn't exist, auth issue), Docker prints a clear error and
  _dev_container will return non-zero. So the current behavior is already
  correct — no extra handling needed.

⏺ Found it! This is a zsh variable modifier issue. In zsh, $image:latest gets
  parsed as ${image:l}atest — where :l is zsh's lowercase modifier, and atest is
   the remaining literal text.

  The fix is to brace-delimit the variable:

⏺ Update(~/.zshrc)
  ⎿  Added 1 line, removed 1 line
      467      "$DEV_CONTAINER_CLI" run -it --rm \
      468          -e HOST_UID="$(id -u)" -e HOST_GID="$(id -g)" -e HOST_
           USER="$(whoami)" \
      469          -v "$src_root":/workspace -w /workspace \
      470 -        "ghcr.io/abitofhelp/$image:latest"                    
      470 +        "ghcr.io/abitofhelp/${image}:latest"                  
      471      popd
      472      echo "Returned to original directory."
      473  }

⏺ $image:latest → ${image}:latest. Zsh was treating :l as a modifier. Copy to
  MBP, source, and try again.

❯ perfect!                                                                      

⏺ Glad that caught it — zsh modifier parsing is sneaky. Let me know how adast
  works on the MBP now.

  (github.com Settings > Developer settings > Personal access tokens).

  But we can switch to the keyring token which already has all the scopes:

  gh auth switch

❯ can we use the ssh identity mike_macpro_gh?                                   

⏺ No — SSH keys are for git operations (clone, push, pull). GitHub Projects API
  requires an OAuth/PAT token with the right scopes. They're separate auth
  mechanisms.

  The quickest fix is switching to your keyring token which already has all the
  needed scopes. Want to try gh auth switch?

⏺ I can't edit .secrets.age — it's age-encrypted and requires the browser to
  regenerate the token at GitHub.

  Here's the process:
  1. Go to github.com > Settings > Developer settings > Personal access tokens
  2. Find the token starting with ghp_
  3. Edit it and add scopes: read:org, read:discussion
  4. Copy the new token
  5. Update it in your secrets source file, re-encrypt with age, and reload

  That's a manual process. Want to just do option 1 (unset GH_TOKEN) for now so
  we can finish the project setup?

❯ So, if we create a new issue in astfmt, will it automatically appear in the   
adafmt project ?                                                                

⏺ No — GitHub Projects don't auto-add issues from linked repos. Each new issue
  needs to be added manually, either through the GitHub UI or via:

  GH_TOKEN="" gh project item-add 2 --owner @me --url <issue_url>

  GitHub does support auto-add workflows via Project settings (built-in
  automation), where you can set a filter like "auto-add issues from repos X, Y,
   Z" — but that requires configuring it in the browser under Project > Settings
   > Workflows > Auto-add to project.

  Want to set that up in the browser, or just add issues manually as we create
  them?

❯ i think we want auto, dont you                                                

⏺ Yes. Set it up in the browser:

  Project > Settings > Workflows > Auto-add to project

  Add a filter for each repo:
  repo:abitofhelp/abohlib,abitofhelp/adafmt,abitofhelp/astfmt,abitofhelp/clara

  That way every new issue in any of those 4 repos appears in the project
  automatically. Once it's configured, we never have to think about it again.

❯ where do i create the filter?                                                 

⏺ In the browser:

  1. Go to your AdaFmt project page
  2. Click the ... menu (top right) > Settings
  3. In the left sidebar, click Workflows
  4. Click Auto-add to project
  5. Toggle it On
  6. In the filter field, enter:
  repo:abitofhelp/abohlib,abitofhelp/adafmt,abitofhelp/astfmt,abitofhelp/clara
  7. Click Save

❯ what is best practice for the titles?  we assign the label for filtering      
purposes.  The prefix to the Title is so we can easily know what kind of issue  
it is without opening it.  Best practice to use the label as a prefix in the    
title of an issue?  If yes, should the prefix be lowercase like the label, or   
capital case, as you did creating the issues?                                   

⏺ Using the label as a title prefix is common and practical — it gives you
  instant context in notifications, CLI output, and email where labels aren't
  visible.

  For casing: capitalize the prefix (e.g., Bug:, Task:, Enhancement:). It's the
  start of a title, not a commit message. Lowercase looks odd at the beginning
  of a sentence. The label stays lowercase for filtering; the prefix is for
  human readability.

  So: label bug + title Bug: trailing comment relocation causes indent 
  instability.

  That's what you already have. Keep it.

⏺ Explore(Find Max_Length_Entries in astfmt)  ⎿  Done (15 tool uses · 40.8k tokens · 46s)
  (ctrl+o to expand)

⏺ Got it — all build/test commands via docker exec dev-container-ada. Good to
  know gdb is available too.

  Now let me read the key files for the P0 bug.

  Read 2 files (ctrl+o to expand)

⏺ Good. Here's the P0 bug analysis:

  Root cause: Formatted_Length_Map in goal_types.ads:39 has Max_Length_Entries =
   10_000. When a large file has more than 10K measurable constructs, Add_Length
   silently drops entries (line 17-21 of goal_types.adb). This means the
  wrap-point analyzer misses constructs, producing incorrect line-break
  decisions.

  Key observations:
  - The map is stack-allocated (local variable in linebreak.adb:274)
  - Each entry is ~24 bytes, so 10K = ~240 KB on the stack
  - Lookup is O(n) linear scan — also a performance concern for large files
  - No warning or error when overflow occurs

  Proposed fix (minimal, safe):

  1. Add Overflow_Detected : Boolean := False to Formatted_Length_Map record
  2. Set it in Add_Length when an entry is dropped
  3. Increase Max_Length_Entries from 10,000 to 50,000 (1.2 MB — workers already
   have large stacks)
  4. Add a check after measurement in the caller to log a warning if overflow
  occurred

  This keeps the bounded design (no heap allocation, deterministic memory), but
  makes overflow visible and much less likely.

  Want me to proceed, or do you want to discuss the approach first?

❯ Since astfmt is non-spark, we have loosened the bounded rule where large      
files are invovled.  Is this a good candidate for the exception to use the      
heap?  If so, please locate another example in astfmt source to compare that    
the use cases are similar... needing variable memory and sometimes a lot of it. 

  Searched for 1 pattern, read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

⏺ Good precedent. Object_Pool uses Ada.Containers.Vectors in the infrastructure
  layer for exactly the same reason — variable, potentially large collections
  where a fixed bound is impractical.

  Yes, this is a good candidate for heap. The use cases are similar:
  - Both are infrastructure layer (SPARK off)
  - Both handle variable-sized data that depends on input file size
  - Both need to grow beyond what a reasonable stack bound can predict
  - Object_Pool uses Vectors for pooled objects; Formatted_Length_Map needs the
  same for measured constructs

  The fix would replace the fixed array with Ada.Containers.Hashed_Maps keyed by
   Source_Location — which also solves the O(n) linear scan in Lookup and
  Contains. Want me to proceed?

❯ Yes, and afterwards, please scan the source code for any similar use cases    
that are still using bounded/stack.  Let's review whether any of them should be 
 heaped, too.  I think the precedent is only the infrastructure layer, correct?

      452  # Detect host architecture once.
      453  ARCH="$(uname -m)"

      455 +# Compute the next available container name for a given image.
      456 +# Queries Docker for running/stopped containers matching the i
          +mage prefix,                                                  
      457 +# finds the highest numeric suffix, and returns prefix-(N+1). 
      458 +_next_container_name() {                                      
      459 +    local image="$1"                                          
      460 +    local max=0 num                                           
      461 +    for name in $("$DEV_CONTAINER_CLI" ps -a --format '{{.Name
          +s}}' | grep "^${image}-[0-9]"); do                            
      462 +        num="${name##*-}"                                     
      463 +        (( num > max )) && max=$num                           
      464 +    done                                                      
      465 +    echo "${image}-$(( max + 1 ))"                            
      466 +}

      481      pushd "$src_root" || return 1
      466 -    echo "Loading $label on $ARCH..."                         
      467 -    "$DEV_CONTAINER_CLI" run -it --rm \                       
      482 +    echo "Loading $label on $ARCH as $cname..."               
      483 +    "$DEV_CONTAINER_CLI" run -it --rm --name "$cname" \       
      484          -e HOST_UID="$(id -u)" -e HOST_GID="$(id -g)" -e HOST_
           USER="$(whoami)" \
      485          -v "$src_root":/workspace -w /workspace \
      486          "ghcr.io/abitofhelp/${image}:latest"
⏺ Done. The function now:
  1. Queries Docker for all containers matching <image>-N
  2. Finds the highest N
  3. Names the new container <image>-(N+1)
  4. Displays the name on launch: "Loading ... as dev-container-ada-1..."

  Since --rm cleans up on exit, the counter effectively resets. If you run two
  concurrently, they'll get -1 and -2.

  Go ahead and kill the current container, source .zshrc, and relaunch with
  adat. It should come up as dev-container-ada-1.

  Inside the container they poison the build with macOS flags.

  The fix: Regenerate these configs inside the container with alr build (which
  overwrites them), or add config/*_config.* to .gitignore so they're never
  committed. Which approach do you prefer? The .gitignore approach is the
  permanent fix — these files are always machine-generated.

❯ good analysis from you and gpt.  please tell me what you think:   Howdy 😄    
                                                                                
I reviewed Claude’s plan against the current astfmt source and your rules. My   
take: the direction is correct and the refactor is justified, but I would not   
implement the draft exactly as written.                                         
                                                                                
The core diagnosis is sound. The plan identifies fixed-size trivia and metadata 
 collections with silent-drop behavior, and it chooses heap-backed containers   
in Infrastructure, which fits your architecture because Infrastructure is where 
 technical storage details belong. Your Ada rules also explicitly allow binary  
projects to opt out of embedded-safe heap restrictions, so using unbounded      
vectors here is not a rules violation.                                          
                                                                                
I would approve the storage refactor itself. I would **not** collapse the Raw → 
 Classified → Owned → Analysis trivia pipeline right now. The plan already      
treats that as a larger refactor, and I agree; the defect is about bounded      
storage and silent truncation, not about the staged model being architecturally 
 wrong.                                                                         
                                                                                
The biggest technical correction I would make is this: use                      
`Ada.Containers.Vectors` with **`Index_Type => Positive`**, not `Natural`. The  
draft cites `Object_Pool` as a vector precedent indexed by `Natural`, but it    
also proposes loops like `for I in 1 .. Natural(Entries.Length)` plus direct    
`Element(I)` and `Reference(I)` access. That migration shape is only naturally  
correct if the new vector stays 1-based. With a `Natural`-indexed vector, the   
first appended element is at index 0, so the draft’s own loop/index examples    
become off-by-one.                                                              
                                                                                
I would also **keep `Empty_Metadata`**. The draft proposes removing it and      
relying on default initialization or `Clear`, but an explicit empty constant    
still has value even when the internals switch to vectors. It preserves intent, 
 reduces churn, and keeps “empty preprocessing result” as a semantic object     
instead of making each caller know how to build one. The plan itself already    
shows multiple callers that would otherwise need special handling.              
                                                                                
On the metadata side, I think the draft underestimates the API blast radius. It 
 says only two `Get_Splits_For` callers need updates, but in the current source 
 the dependency chain is wider than that because the visitor facade and the     
string-literal path still lean on array/sentinel-style behavior. So I would     
either keep the visitor-facing API stable and adapt internally, or change the   
public split API deliberately and update every dependent site in one pass. As   
written, that part of the checklist is too optimistic.                          
                                                                                
I would also simplify the proposed compatibility layer. `Entry_Count(C)` is     
fine. `Get_Entry` might be fine. But `Set_Entry_Field(C, I, ...)` is an         
abstraction tax. It tries to fake array-field syntax instead of letting the new 
 container model be real. Since this is infrastructure-internal code, I would   
keep only a very small helper surface and otherwise use direct vector           
operations.                                                                     
                                                                                
The file list should be corrected before anyone starts. The draft’s trivia and  
metadata test lists are incomplete for the actual source tree, so the           
implementation plan will otherwise look “finished” while leaving obvious        
compile/test fallout behind.                                                    
                                                                                
One thing I do agree with strongly is the choice to use `Reference` for         
`.Emitted` mutations. That is cleaner than copy/replace, and the risk note is   
reasonable as long as those loops do not structurally modify the vector while a 
 reference is live.                                                             
                                                                                
On `Reserve_Capacity`, I would make it data-driven, not a hardcoded `1000`. The 
 question is good; the fixed hint is not. For trivia, reserve from cheap        
observed counts if available. For metadata, profile first and keep the first    
correctness refactor simple.                                                    
                                                                                
I would also add a documentation step. Your rules require SDS/STP and related   
docs to stay current when design and test strategy change, and this refactor    
changes both the storage design and the test surface.                           
                                                                                
So my recommendation is:                                                        
                                                                                
Approve the refactor, but revise Claude’s plan before implementation:           
                                                                                
1. Trivia collections first.                                                    
2. Use vectors with `Index_Type => Positive`.                                   
3. Keep the staged trivia pipeline.                                             
4. Keep `Empty_Metadata`.                                                       
5. Either preserve the visitor split API or widen the change list honestly.     
6. Trim the compatibility-accessor idea down to the minimum.                    
7. Update docs along with tests.                                                
                                                                                
Net: **yes to the refactor, no to the draft exactly as written**.               
                                                                                

⏺ GPT's review is excellent. I agree with every correction. Here's my
  assessment:

  Critical fix — Index_Type => Positive: GPT is right and I was wrong. The
  entire codebase uses 1-based indexing (for I in 1 .. Entry_Count). Using
  Natural (0-based) would introduce off-by-one bugs at every caller. This was a
  real defect in my plan.

  Keep Empty_Metadata: Agreed. It's a semantic constant expressing intent. Easy
  to implement as a function returning a record with an empty vector. Eliminates
   churn at 5+ call sites.

  Metadata API blast radius: GPT caught a gap I missed. I said "2 callers" for
  Get_Splits_For but the visitor facade and string-literal path create a wider
  dependency chain. I need to either stabilize the public API or honestly widen
  the change list.

  Trim Set_Entry_Field: Agreed. It's abstraction tax. Direct Reference(I) and
  Element(I) are cleaner for infrastructure-internal code. Keep only Entry_Count
   as a helper.

  Reserve_Capacity data-driven: Good call. Hardcoded 1000 is a guess.
  Correctness first, optimize later.

  Documentation step: Missing from my plan and required by our rules.

  File list incomplete: Needs verification before starting.

  Want me to revise the plan now with all of GPT's corrections incorporated?

          -ntial append + indexed read |

          - append + linear search (multi-value per key rules out hashed 
          -map) |

       68

       75 -

          -indexed iteration                                             
       77 -  is the primary pattern, not key-based lookup.               
       78 -- `Trivia_Analysis` entries are mutated in-place (`.Emitted :=
          - True`) during                                                
       79 -  emission — Vectors support this via `Reference(Index)`.     
       69 +- The trivia pipeline processes entries **in source order** — 
          +indexed                                                       
       70 +  iteration is the primary pattern, not key-based lookup.     
       71 +- `Trivia_Analysis` entries are mutated in-place (`.Emitted :=
          + True`)                                                       
       72 +  during emission — Vectors support this via `Reference(Index)
          +`.                                                            
       73  - `LineBreak_Metadata` allows multiple split points per `Sourc
           e_Location`
       74    (multi-map), so a single-key hashed map would require a valu
           e type of
       75    `Vector` anyway. A flat `Vector` with linear search is simpl
           er and
       76    sufficient for the observed cardinalities.

          +h the

          +_Pool`

      105 +### D5: Minimal Compatibility Layer                           
      106  
      110 -### In-Place Mutation (`Emitted` field)                       
      107 +Only `Entry_Count(C)` is provided as a convenience function. N
          +o                                                             
      108 +`Get_Entry` or `Set_Entry_Field` wrappers. Callers use direct 
          +vector                                                        
      109 +operations (`Element(I)`, `Reference(I)`, `Append`). This avoi
          +ds                                                            
      110 +abstraction tax and lets the container model be real. Since th
          +is is                                                         
      111 +infrastructure-internal code, the direct API is appropriate.  
      112  
      113 +### D6: `Reference` for In-Place Mutation                     
      114 +                                                              
      115  The emitter sets `Analysis.Entries(I).Emitted := True` at 7 lo
           cations.
      113 -With Vectors, this becomes:                                   
      116 +With Vectors:                                                 
      117  
      118  ```ada
      116 -declare                                                       
      117 -   E : Trivia_Entry := Analysis.Entries.Element (I);          
      118 -begin                                                         
      119 -   E.Emitted := True;                                         
      120 -   Analysis.Entries.Replace_Element (I, E);                   
      121 -end;                                                          
      122 -```                                                           
      123 -                                                              
      124 -Alternatively, use `Reference`:                               
      125 -```ada                                                        
      119  Analysis.Entries.Reference (I).Emitted := True;
      120  ```
      121  
      129 -The `Reference` approach is cleaner and avoids the copy. Recom
          -mend using                                                    
      130 -`Reference` for all `.Emitted` mutations.                     
      122 +This is cleaner than copy/replace and safe because all `.Emitt
          +ed`                                                           
      123 +mutations happen during single-pass iteration with no vector i
          +nsertions.                                                    
      124  
      125 +### D7: No Hardcoded Reserve_Capacity                         
      126 +                                                              
      127 +The first implementation uses default vector growth (start sma
          +ll, double                                                    
      128 +on realloc). Adding `Reserve_Capacity` hints is deferred until
          + profiling                                                    
      129 +data is available. Correctness first, optimize later.         
      130 +                                                              
      131 +### D8: `Get_Splits_For` Returns a Vector                     
      132 +                                                              
      133 +The return type changes from `Split_Point_Array(1..Max_Split_P
          +oints)` to                                                    
      134 +`Split_Vectors.Vector`. This is a deliberate API change that m
          +ust be                                                        
      135 +propagated to all callers in a single pass:                   
      136 +                                                              
      137 +- `metadata.ads/adb` — function signature and implementation  
      138 +- `visitor.ads/adb` — `Get_Split_Points` wrapper return type  
      139 +- `literals.adb` — string literal handler (primary consumer)  
      140 +- `test_preprocessing_metadata.adb` — test assertions         
      141 +- `test_visitor.adb` — test assertions                        
      142 +                                                              
      143 +The string literal handler currently uses a sentinel pattern  
      144 +(`exit when Splits(I).Insert_Length = 0`) to detect unused arr
          +ay slots.                                                     
      145 +With a Vector, this becomes natural iteration over actual elem
          +ents —                                                        
      146 +the sentinel is eliminated, simplifying the code.

❯ almost there! :D   from gpt: Howdy 😄                                         
                                                                                
This revision is **much better**. It fixed the big problems from the first      
draft: it now explicitly chooses `Index_Type => Positive`, keeps the staged     
trivia pipeline, keeps `Empty_Metadata`, drops the fake compatibility wrapper   
idea, and makes the `Get_Splits_For` API change explicit. That is a real        
improvement, not cosmetic.                                                      
                                                                                
It also fits your rules well enough for this project. Your Ada standards prefer 
 stack allocation in general, but they also explicitly allow executable         
projects to opt out of embedded restrictions and permit heap-backed collections 
 when that is the right engineering choice. For astfmt, this refactor is in     
Infrastructure and is solving real correctness limits, so the direction is      
defensible.                                                                     
                                                                                
My verdict: **almost ready, but not quite “approved as-is.”**                   
I would make **2 required edits** before implementation.                        
                                                                                
## Required edits                                                               
                                                                                
**1) Fix every `Positive (Vector.Length)` loop pattern.**                       
                                                                                
The plan now repeatedly says things like:                                       
                                                                                
* `for I in 1 .. Positive (Result.Entries.Length) loop`                         
* `for I in 1 .. Positive (Input.Entries.Length) loop`                          
* `for I in 1 .. Positive (Meta.Split_Points.Length) loop`                      
                                                                                
That is unsafe on an empty vector, because `Positive (0)` raises                
`Constraint_Error` before the loop even starts.                                 
                                                                                
Use one of these instead:                                                       
                                                                                
* `for I in 1 .. Entry_Count (...) loop` and cast only at access time           
* guard with `if not Entries.Is_Empty then`                                     
* use a cursor-based loop                                                       
                                                                                
This is not theoretical; the current repo has plenty of empty/default paths and 
 tests.                                                                         
                                                                                
**2) Remove the “mutate in query functions” bullet in Step 1.2.**               
                                                                                
The revised plan says:                                                          
                                                                                
* “Use `Result.Entries.Reference(I).Emitted` for mutation in query functions”   
                                                                                
That should not be in the analyzer query functions. Those routines are          
read-only by design. `Emitted := True` belongs in the emitter and other `in     
out` mutation sites, not in the analyzer query API. As written, that bullet is  
conceptually wrong and invites accidental signature drift.                      
                                                                                
## Minor polish                                                                 
                                                                                
A few smaller things I’d tighten:                                               
                                                                                
* In D7, replace “start small, double on realloc” with a more neutral           
statement. Amortized append is fine; exact growth policy is implementation      
detail.                                                                         
* In the risk table, I would remove “Net positive from removing O(n) linear     
scans.” This refactor mainly fixes bounded-capacity loss and stack pressure; it 
 does **not** fundamentally remove metadata linear search.                      
* Phase 2 says “src: 6 files” but then lists **7** source files. Tiny doc bug,  
but worth fixing before implementation.                                         
                                                                                
## Bottom line                                                                  
                                                                                
This updated plan is now **good enough in direction and structure** that I’d    
green-light it **after those two required edits**. The architecture choice is   
sound, the scope is much more honest, and the implementation sequence is        
sensible.                                                                       
                                                                                
If you want, I can also draft the exact wording changes for those two plan      
edits so Claude can patch the document cleanly.

❯ woohoo!  see what you think... :)  Howdy again 😄                             
                                                                                
This version is the first one I’d call **substantively approved**. The major    
issues are now fixed: it keeps the staged trivia pipeline, keeps                
`Empty_Metadata`, uses `Index_Type => Positive`, removes the fake               
compatibility-wrapper idea, switches `Get_Splits_For` to a vector deliberately, 
 and rewrites the metadata loops to use `Entry_Count (Meta)` instead of the     
unsafe `Positive (Length)` pattern. That is the right shape technically.        
                                                                                
It also fits your standards. The refactor is contained in Infrastructure, and   
your architecture rules explicitly allow Infrastructure to own technical        
storage details; your Ada rules also allow executable projects to opt out of    
embedded restrictions when that is the better engineering tradeoff, including   
heap-backed/unbounded collections.                                              
                                                                                
So my answer now is: **yes, this is ready to implement**.                       
I only see **one remaining documentation nit**, not a design blocker.           
                                                                                
The nit is in the bookkeeping: the Phase 2 narrative explicitly says            
`orchestrator.ads` must be updated for the `Empty_Metadata` change, but the     
Phase 2 “Files Modified (Complete List)” section does not list                  
`orchestrator.ads`. Since that file is already listed in Phase 1, this is       
probably just a cross-phase accounting mismatch, not a real implementation      
problem. I would either add a note saying the metadata-related orchestrator     
adjustment is absorbed into the Phase 1 edit, or include it in the Phase 2 list 
 as well.                                                                       
                                                                                
A couple of things are especially solid now:                                    
                                                                                
The plan correctly treats this as a **bounded-storage correctness refactor**,   
not a stealth redesign of the trivia pipeline. That restraint is good.          
                                                                                
The `Reference` choice for `.Emitted := True` is the right one for the emitter  
path, and the plan’s safety rationale is sound because it limits that mutation  
to single-pass iteration without insertions.                                    
                                                                                
The metadata API change is now honest. Returning `Split_Vectors.Vector` and     
updating `visitor`, `literals`, and the related tests in one pass is much       
cleaner than preserving the old sentinel-array contract.                        
                                                                                
The performance language is also healthier now. It defers `Reserve_Capacity`    
until profiling instead of guessing, which matches your “correctness first,     
optimize later” standard.                                                       
                                                                                
Bottom line: **green light**.                                                   
I’d let Claude proceed after that one file-list cleanup, but even if he forgot  
that doc tweak, I would not stop implementation over it.

  Now to your MBP build error — you're hitting a missing libiconv on arm64:

  cannot find -liconv: No such file or directory

  This is the adast system container using GNAT 15.2.1 via Alire (not the apt
  GNAT 13.3.0). The Alire toolchain on arm64 needs libiconv-dev installed. Try:

  # Inside the container:

❯ i am interested in what happens when we build the images again in the future. 
  any required fixes need to be made to the scripts.  we need to ensure that

⏺ Good point. The Dockerfile already has alr toolchain --select gnat_external at
   image build time (line 239), but Alire's config can drift at runtime when alr
   build auto-resolves dependencies and pulls a newer toolchain. That's what
  happened — Alire silently downloaded GNAT 15.2.1 inside the running container.

  Two fixes to consider for the Dockerfiles:

  1. Pin the toolchain selection in entrypoint.sh — re-run alr toolchain 
  --select gnat_external on every container start, not just image build
  2. Add alr config --global --set toolchain.assistant false — prevents Alire
  from auto-downloading toolchains at runtime

  But this is a separate task from the Vector refactor. Want me to create an
  issue for it so we can address it properly later? The containers work fine
  once you run alr toolchain --select gnat_external manually.

❯ i think that we already did 2.  is   the choice 1. or 2.    or    1 and 2?    

  Searched for 2 patterns (ctrl+o to expand)

⏺ We haven't done 2 yet. The answer is both 1 and 2:

  - 2 prevents Alire from ever auto-downloading a toolchain at runtime
  - 1 ensures the correct toolchain is selected even if the config drifts

  But this is a container image fix, not part of the Vector refactor. Want me to
   create an issue for it?

⏺ That fixes it. The release build needs -XLIBRARY_TYPE=static on amd64 because
  the Alire-managed dependencies only have static libraries.

  Two options:
  1. Add -XLIBRARY_TYPE=static to ALR_BUILD_FLAGS in the Makefile (affects all
  platforms)
  2. Make it conditional on architecture in the Makefile

  Since arm64 works without it (system libraries have both types), what do you
  prefer?

✻ Crunched for 53s

❯ best practice is my choice.  Unless there is a reason for static on all       
platforms, I'd use 2.  At some point, we will need to build distributable       
binary executables of adafmt, so keep this in mind if it is related to this     
issue.                                                                          
⏺ For distributable binaries, static linking is what you want — it produces a
  self-contained executable with no shared library dependencies. Users don't
  need to install deps26, Alire, or any Ada runtime.

  So the best practice for a distributable CLI tool like adafmt is: release 
  builds should always use static linking, regardless of platform. Development
  builds can use whatever's available (faster incremental linking with shared
  libs if they exist).

  This means option 1 is actually the right choice — but only for release mode:

  - build-dev / build — no LIBRARY_TYPE override (use whatever's default)
  - build-release — force -XLIBRARY_TYPE=static (distributable binary)

  Want me to update the adafmt Makefile with this?

❯ will this break the correct building using dev_container_ada docker inmage?   
we worked hard to get tyhe toolchain stuff to work properly...                  

⏺ Good call to pause. The alire.lock file is the issue — it's per-platform but
  shared via the bind mount. If we delete it and Alire regenerates for macOS,
  then the container will get the macOS lock file and break.

  This is fundamentally the same problem as the config files — the lock file is
  host-specific but lives in the shared source directory.

  Options:
  1. Add alire/alire.lock to .gitignore — each environment regenerates its own.
  But the bind mount still shares one copy between host and container.
  2. Don't build on macOS host — always use the container. The macOS toolchain
  isn't needed if the container works.
  3. Separate workspaces — macOS host uses a different clone than the container
  mount.

  Since you're always building inside the container, option 2 is the simplest —
  don't try to alr build on the macOS host. The host is for editing and git; the
   container is for building.

  Does that make sense, or do you need macOS-native builds?

❯ the issue is that it is easy to use the dev_container_add to build for arm64  
and amd64, but they produce linux binaries, not macos.  As far as I know, there 
 is no way to create a docker image for dev_container_ada for macos. or any     
docker image with macos as its host. am i wrong?                                

⏺ You're right — Docker cannot run macOS containers. Docker on Mac runs Linux
  VMs. So:

  - Container builds → Linux binaries (amd64 or arm64)
  - macOS native builds → macOS binaries

  If you want distributable macOS binaries, you need to build on the macOS host
  directly. The lock file conflict is the blocker.

  The cleanest fix: add alire/alire.lock to .gitignore and accept that each
  environment regenerates it. The bind mount issue (host and container sharing
  the same directory) means you'd need to delete the lock file when switching
  between host and container builds. That's a manual step but it's quick:

  # Before building on macOS host:
  rm -f alire/alire.lock

  # Before building in container:
  rm -f alire/alire.lock

  Or we could script it into the Makefile — detect the platform and delete the
  lock file if the toolchain hash doesn't match.

  What do you prefer?

❯ so, it is crucial to inform ... document that building Ada for a specific     
platform must be done synchronously when using a single host computer.          
Otherwise, the builds will conflict on the alire.lock file.  correct?           

⏺ Correct. On a single machine with both macOS-native and Linux-container builds
   sharing the same source directory via bind mount, only one platform can own 
  the Alire lock file at a time. Switching platforms requires regenerating the
  lock.

  This is a fundamental constraint of Alire's design — the lock file captures
  platform-specific toolchain resolution (OS, arch, toolchain hash) and lives
  alongside the source.

  Want me to document this in a BUILD_PLATFORMS.md or add a section to the
  existing REORIENTATION.md / README.md?

❯ For now, I think this goes in the build section of README.md.  This is an FYI 
 that the dev cannot try to do builds concurrently on the same system to save   
time.  Won't work and the binaries, if produced, will be wonky.                 

⏺ Let me check the current README build section:

  Searched for 1 pattern, read 1 file (ctrl+o to expand)

❯ we keep bumping into the issue that when a build fails, it will fail silently 
 with the grep filter we are currently using.  My memory is that we corrected   
this issue in one of the 13 active ada project for adafmt.  Pls scan the 13     
project makefiles and compare the build and grep used.  See if we find the      
corrected version, otherwise, we need to figure out a better way to filter out  
build noise except for style and warning and of course error.                   

⏺ Bash(for repo in abohlib adafmt astfmt clara corpus_ada deps26 functional
      hybrid_app_ada hybrid_app_docs hybrid_lib_ada hybrid_lib_docs

     (eval):1: command not found: head
     === adafmt ===

⏺ Now let me check the other repos:

  Searched for 4 patterns (ctrl+o to expand)

⏺ All 5 Ada repos with Makefiles use the same pattern — || true at the end
  swallows the exit code. None have a corrected version. The problem is the same
   everywhere:

  The issue: alr build ... 2>&1 | grep ... || true
  - The | grep changes the exit code to grep's exit code (0 if matched, 1 if
  not)
  - The || true ensures make never sees a failure
  - So even if alr build returns exit code 4 (compilation failed), make sees
  success

  The fix: Capture the build output and exit code separately, filter for
  display, then propagate the original exit code. Something like:

  ALR_BUILD_FLAGS := -XGNATCOLL_ICONV_OPT= -j0
  ALR_BUILD_FILTER := 2>&1 | grep -E
  'warning:|error:|\(style\)|finished|Success' || true

  # In targets:
  build: check-arch prereqs
        @echo "Building..."
        @$(ALR) build --development -- $(ALR_BUILD_FLAGS); \
        EXIT=$$?; \
        [ $$EXIT -ne 0 ] && echo "$(RED)Build FAILED (exit code $$EXIT)$(NC)" &&
  $$EXIT; \
        echo "$(GREEN)✓ Build complete$(NC)"

  Or simpler — use pipefail so the pipe propagates the first failure:

        @set -o pipefail && $(ALR) build --development -- $(ALR_BUILD_FLAGS) 2>&
  grep -E 'warning:|error:|\(style\)|finished|Success'

  The set -o pipefail approach is cleanest. Want me to apply it across both
  adafmt and astfmt?

✻ Sautéed for 55s

❯ which is a best practice                                                      

⏺ set -o pipefail is the best practice — it's the POSIX-standard way to
  propagate failure through pipes. Used widely in CI/CD, Docker, and production
  shell scripts.

  Want me to apply it to adafmt and astfmt now? The other repos (hybrid_lib_ada,
   hybrid_app_ada, functional, clara) are shared templates — those should be
  fixed in the source repo per the submodule rules.

❯ Yes, let's make the change to the active projects.  the gitmodule related     
project need to have the change, too.  It is a fundamental build feature for    
ada projects.                                                                   

⏺ Let me design this properly. The fix needs to:
  1. Separate build flags from the output filter
  2. Use set -o pipefail so build failures propagate
  3. Use { grep ... || true; } so grep's no-match doesn't trigger a false
  failure

  ⎿  Interrupted · What should Claude do instead?

❯ i don't want to change the makefiles from zsh to bash just to use pipefail    

⏺ Fair point. Let me use a different approach that works with any POSIX shell.
  Instead of pipefail, capture the exit code explicitly:

  ALR_BUILD_FLAGS := -XGNATCOLL_ICONV_OPT= -j0
  ALR_OUTPUT_FILTER = 2>&1; EXIT=$$?; [ $$EXIT -ne 0 ] && exit $$EXIT; true

  Wait — that loses the filtering. Let me think...

  The simplest POSIX approach: write output to a temp file, check exit code,
  then filter the file:

  @$(ALR) build --development -- $(ALR_BUILD_FLAGS) > /tmp/alr_build.log 2>&1; \
  EXIT=$$?; \
  grep -E 'warning:|error:|\(style\)|finished|Success' /tmp/alr_build.log ||
  true; \
  exit $$EXIT

  This works in any shell, preserves the exit code, and still filters the
  output. Want me to use this approach instead?

❯ why not create a function that wraps what must be done?  seems cleaner        

⏺ Yes — a shell function or a script. A small wrapper script in scripts/ would
  be cleanest since Makefile inline functions get ugly. Something like:

  scripts/alr-build.sh:
  #!/bin/sh
  # Run an Alire build command, filter output to diagnostics only,
  # and propagate the build exit code.
  "$@" > /tmp/alr_build_$$.log 2>&1
  EXIT=$?
  grep -E 'warning:|error:|\(style\)|finished|Success' /tmp/alr_build_$$.log ||
  true
  rm -f /tmp/alr_build_$$.log
  exit $EXIT

  Then the Makefile becomes:
  ALR_BUILD_FLAGS := -XGNATCOLL_ICONV_OPT= -j0
  ALR_BUILD = scripts/alr-build.sh $(ALR)

  # Usage:
        @$(ALR_BUILD) build --development -- $(ALR_BUILD_FLAGS)

  Clean, portable, reusable across all projects. Want me to implement this?

❯ a python script would be a good fit, too.  it is usually the first choice for 
 new scripts                                                                    

⏺ True — Python is our standard for scripting, and it handles cross-platform
  better. Plus we already have scripts/python/ in every project.

  scripts/python/alr_build.py:
  #!/usr/bin/env python3
  """Run an Alire build command, filter output to diagnostics, propagate exit 
  code."""

  import re
  import subprocess
  import sys

  FILTER = re.compile(r"warning:|error:|\(style\)|finished|Success")

  result = subprocess.run(sys.argv[1:], capture_output=True, text=True)

  for line in (result.stdout + result.stderr).splitlines():
      if FILTER.search(line):
          print(line)

  sys.exit(result.returncode)

  Then in Makefiles:
  ALR_BUILD_FLAGS := -XGNATCOLL_ICONV_OPT= -j0
  ALR_BUILD = python3 scripts/python/alr_build.py $(ALR)

        @$(ALR_BUILD) build --development -- $(ALR_BUILD_FLAGS)

  Since this is reusable across all Ada projects, should it go in
  hybrid_scripts_python (the shared submodule)?

❯ i agree

  there:
